Chapter of Analogy. Definition of the Sign. As for the sign, it is that which indicates existence without any obligation or existence being attached to it. It is sometimes called a condition, like ihsan in the chapter of zina, for when it is established, it is an identifier for the ruling of zina. However, it is not so that the zina exists in its form and its being a cause is contingent upon the existence of ihsan. (That is, zina.) For if both conditions are found in ownership, such as if she entered the two houses while in his marriage, then without doubt the consequence descends and divorce occurs by agreement. And if they are not found in ownership, such as if he divorced her and then she entered the two houses, or if the first is found in ownership but not the second, such as if she entered one house while in his marriage then he divorced her and she entered the other—this is like the one who divorces by agreement. And if the second is found in ownership but not the first, such as if he divorced her and she entered one house, then he married her and she entered the other, there is a difference of opinion: divorce occurs according to us because the consequence descends; for the consideration is on the last condition, and the need is for ownership at the time of the suspension and at the time of the consequence, and ownership exists at both times. As for what is between, ownership does not exist and there is no need for it. According to Zufar, she is not divorced because the two conditions are one thing for the obligation of the consequence; just as in one of them ownership is required, so in the other. So if ownership does not exist in the first, divorce does not occur, just as it does not occur if ownership exists in the first but not the second by agreement. The fifth type: a condition in the sense of a sign, like ihsan in zina. The author left these two divisions, although the mention of the sign suffices for the fifth. The sign: In language, it is the mark, like the milestone for the road and the minaret for the mosque. In sacred law, it is what he explained by his saying: 'that which indicates existence' i.e., the existence of the ruling, and by this he excluded the cause. 'Obligation': i.e., the obligation of the ruling, and by this he excluded the effective cause. 'Nor existence of the ruling': by this he excluded the condition. So the sign is a pure indicator of the existence of the ruling when it exists, and it is merely a marker, like the call to prayer: it is a sign of the prayer. Condition: metaphorically, it is the fifth division of condition; for it is in reality a sign but it is called a condition metaphorically. The ruling of zina: i.e., stoning, so it is a state of the adulterer. And it is evidence that when zina exists in that state, stoning becomes necessary, and it is not a condition of the ruling of zina as he explained by his saying: 'However it is not so that...' i.e., if ihsan were a condition for the ruling of zina, which is stoning, while the reality is that zina is the cause of stoning, then the existence of zina as a cause would be contingent on the existence of ihsan, which is not the case. For if ihsan occurs after zina, its existence does not establish stoning. If it were a condition, stoning would be established by its existence. Therefore, when zina, which is the cause, exists, and then ihsan exists—according to your claim a condition—its occurrence after the cause would necessitate that with all this, the ruling is not established. So it is proven that it is not a condition. And it is known that it is also not an effective cause nor a cause, because it is not a path leading to it. Hence, it is inevitably a sign. Correct. So: This is what Qadi Imam Abu Zaid went to in al-Taqwim, and some later scholars chose it. As for the early scholars and most later ones, they called ihsan a condition for the obligation of stoning, because the condition of a thing is that on which its existence depends, and ihsan is like that. And its preceding the existence of zina does not contradict that, because the delay of conditions after the form of the cause is not necessary; rather, some conditions precede it, like the condition of prayer and witnesses of marriage. Some scholars went to the view that it is a condition having the meaning of a sign. And hence (i.e., because ihsan is a sign and not a real condition) if they retract in any state, i.e., if a people testify against a man that he committed zina, then others testify that he was muhsan, and he is stoned; if the witnesses of ihsan retract, there is no liability (the blood money) upon them in any state, whether they retract with the witnesses of zina or alone, before judgment or after; because they were witnesses of the sign, and the sign has no obligation or existence attached to it, so it is not permissible to attribute the ruling to it in any way. Since stoning is not attributed to the sign, which is ihsan, the witnesses of ihsan are innocent of it, so there is no liability upon them, contrary to Zufar, who holds that they are liable; because ihsan is a condition of stoning, so the ruling is attributed to it. The answer is that it is not a condition as we said, so it is not permissible to attribute the ruling to it. And even if we concede that it is a condition as the early scholars held, when there exists a cause suitable for the ruling, the ruling is not attributed to the condition. So the witnesses of zina are witnesses of the cause, which is suitable for the ruling, so the destruction is attributed to them, and thus liability falls specifically upon them if they retract from the testimony. If they persist, the ruling is cut off by their testimony regarding the condition.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the term 'alamah (sign/indicator) in usul al-fiqh, distinguishing it from shart (condition), sabab (cause), and 'illah (effective cause). The author explains that an 'alamah is a pure indicator of the existence of a ruling, without any causal link. The example of ihsan (being muhsan, i.e., married and free) in the case of zina is used: ihsan is not a condition for stoning, but merely a sign that the ruling of stoning applies when zina occurs under that state. The commentary then presents a detailed discussion comparing the views of early and later Hanafi scholars on whether ihsan is a condition or a sign. A practical application is given: if witnesses of ihsan retract, they are not liable under the Hanafi view because ihsan is a sign, not a condition. This is contrasted with the position of Zufar. The passage also mentions the five types of conditions and the metaphorical use of 'condition' for signs.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-'alamah): A pure indicator that a ruling exists, without any causal connection (no obligation or existence attached).
الشرط (al-shart): A condition on which the existence of a ruling depends; sometimes used metaphorically for 'alamah.
الإحصان (al-ihsan): The state of being muhsan (married and free) which is a sign (not a condition) for stoning in zina.
زفر (Zufar): A Hanafi scholar (Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl) who held that ihsan is a condition for stoning, leading to liability on its witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, why are witnesses of ihsan not liable upon retraction?
A) Because they can retract anytime without consequence.
B) Because ihsan is a sign, not a condition, so the ruling is not attributed to it.
C) Because the witnesses of zina are solely responsible.
D) Because the penalty of stoning is waived if testimony is retracted.

Key Takeaway
The classification of ihsan as an 'alamah rather than a shart determines that its witnesses bear no legal liability, illustrating the practical impact of usul categories.

Jest in Sale Price: Amount vs. Type – A Hanafi Usul Analysis
Explaining Abu Hanifa's view on jest in sale price and comparison with marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between jest in the amount and jest in the genus of the sale price, state the Hanafi position in both cases, and explain the qiyas to marriage and why it is rejected.

Core Idea
Jest in price amount creates a void condition invalidating sale; jest in genus does not – the key is combinability of seriousness and jest.

This passage from a usul al-fiqh text explores the effect of jest (hazl) in the sale price, a subtle issue that tests the boundaries of contract validity. The author presents the Hanafi position of Imam Abu Hanifa, the dissenting view of his two companions (the Sahibayn), and the crucial distinction between jest affecting the amount versus the type of consideration. By working through this analysis, you will learn how the Hanafi school applies the concept of void conditions and why sale differs from marriage in this regard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Cases and Four Scenarios
Recognize that the passage discusses two distinct situations: jest in the amount (qadr) of the price and jest in the genus (jins) of the price. For each, understand the four possible attitudes of the parties: build on the jest, ignore it, remain silent, or differ.
Focus on the first case (amount) as it contains the main ikhtilaf.
2
Extract Abu Hanifa's Ruling
Note that Abu Hanifa consistently upholds the stated price (tasmiya) in all scenarios of jest in amount, except when both parties ignore the jest (then stated price by consensus). In jest in genus, the stated price is valid universally.
His reasoning: the jest creates a void condition that invalidates the sale unless explicitly ignored.
3
Extract the Sahibayn's Ruling and Reasoning
The Sahibayn hold that in jest in amount, the actual agreed price (the one under the jest) is effective; the extra is a void condition that does not invalidate because it is not demanded. In jest in genus, they agree with Abu Hanifa.
Their key argument: it is possible to combine seriousness in the contract with jest in the amount.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Abu Hanifa responds that the extra amount is a positive condition, not mere silence; it is a void condition that invalidates a sale, unlike marriage where void conditions are overlooked.
The distinction hinges on the nature of the contract: sale is strict, marriage is lenient.
5
Compare with Marriage and Identify the Illa
Observe that the Sahibayn analogize sale to marriage, where jest in mahr does not invalidate. Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy because marriage tolerates void conditions; sale does not. The effective cause (illa) is the different legal frameworks.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) where the distinction is based on the primary purpose of the contract.

Source Text

عوارض مكتسبة
بمائة دينار على أن يكون الثمن ألف درهم فالهزل باطل، والتسمية صحيحة في الفصلين عند أبي حنيفة له، وقال صاحباه يصح البيع بألف درهم في الفصل الأول، وبمائة دينار في الفصل الثاني؛ لإمكان العمل بالمواضعة في الثمن مع الجد في أصل العقد في الفصل الأول دون الثاني، وإنا نقول بأنهما جدا في أصل العقد
الفصل

أي قبول بعض البدل
أحــــا
بمائة دينار : هذا نظير للهزل في جنس العوض والتسمية صحيحة إلخ المراد بالفصل الأول هو الهزل في قدر الثمن بأن سميا في العقد ألفين عند الناس والثمن في الحقيقة ،ألف ففي هذه الصورة لايخلو الحال عن الأقسام الأربعة، فإن أعرضا أي اتفقا على الإعراض عن المواضعة بالهزل صح العقد، وكان الثمن هو المسمّى وهو الألفان بالاتفاق، أو سكتا أي اتفقا على أنه لم يحضرهما شيء من البناء والإعراض، أو اختلفا في الإعراض والبناء، فالمعتبر عند أبي حنيفة رحله التسمية وهو ألفان، وقال صاحباه يعتبر المواضعة فكان الثمن هو الألف، و بطل الألف الذي هزلا به، أو بنيا أي اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة بالهزل فالمعتبر عنده المسمّى وهو وعندهما الألف، وهذا ما بينه المصنف في المتن والمراد بالفصل الثاني هو الهزل في جنس الثمن بأن تواضعا على التسمية عند الناس بمائة دينار، ويكون الثمن في الواقع ألف درهم صح البيع وكان الثمن هو المسمّى، وهو مائة دينار بالاتفاق على كل من الأحوال الأربعة.
الفان
في الفصل الثاني والحاصل إنما الاختلاف في الفصل الأول دون الثاني، فعندهما في الفصل الأول يجب الألف. في أصل العقد إلخ يعني لا تعارض بين المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد وبين المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار الثمن، فيمكن الجمع بينهما بأن يجعل العقد منعقداً في الألف الذي في ضمن الألفين ويبطل الألف الآخر الذي هزلا به؛ لأنه غير مطالب لاتفاقهما على الهزل وكل شرط لا مطالب له من العباد لا يفسد به العقد، ولا حاجة إلى اعتبار هذا الألف في تصحيح العقد، فكان ذكره والسكوت العقد، فكان ذكره والسكوت عنه سواء كما في النكاح، فإنه لو تزوجها على ألفين هازلاً والمهر في الواقع ألف ثم اتفقا على البناء على الهزل السابق فالمهر ألف اتفاقاً. الثاني: إذ لا يمكن الجمع بين المواضعة بالهزل في جنس الثمن وبين المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد؛ لأن المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد يقتضي صحة العقد، والمواضعة بالهزل في جنس الثمن يقتضي خلو العقد عن الثمن في البيع؛ لأن المذكور هو مائة دينار، وهي ليست مثمناً لأجل الهزل، والألف المقصود لم تذكر، والثمن ما يذكر في العقد، وخلوّ العقد عن الثمن يفسد البيع، فلا بد أن يترك أحدهما، فتركنا المواضعة بالهزل في جنس الثمن، وأخذنا بالجد في العقد ترجيحاً لجانب المصحح بأنهما جداً إلخ: حيث قصدا بيعاً جائزاً.
فيفسد البيع، فكان العمل بالأصل أولى من العمل بالوصف عند تعارض المواضعتين فيهما، وهذا بخلاف النكاح حيث يجب الأقل بالإجماع؛ لأنّ النكاح لا يفسد بالشرط الفاسد
فيفسد البيع وحاصل جواب أبي حنيفة له أن قولكم (وهو إمكان الجمع بين المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار الثمن وبين المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد غير مسلّم؛ لأنه يمكن الجمع بينهما كما لا يمكن في الفصل الثاني؛ إذ المواضعة بالهزل في مقدار البدل، وهو الثمن تجعل اشتراط قبول الألف الزائد الذي خرج عن الثمنية بالمواضعة شرطاً فاسداً للعقد، لا بمنزلة اشتراط قبول ما ليس من مقتضيات العقد، وهو شرط فاسد يفسد البيع، مع أن فيه للطالب وإن لم يطلبه؛ لأن عدم الطلب بواسطة الرضاء لا يفيد الصحة كالرضى بالربا، وفيه اندفاع لما قـالا بــه والمواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد يقتضي صحة العقد، فإذا لم يمكن الجمع بينهما اخترنا المواضعة بالجد في أصل العقد؛ لأنها مواضعة في الأصل، وهو العقد وتركنا المواضعة في قدر الثمن؛ إذ هي مواضعة في الوصف. فيهما: أي في الأصل والوصف، وقد عرفت تعارض المواضعتين فيهما.
لما
نفعاً
فرغ من القسم الأول من الإنشاء وهو ما يحتمل النقض شرع في القسم الثاني، وهو ما لا يحتمل النقض، وهو على ثلاثة أقسام: القسم الأول: ما كان المال فيه تبعا كالنكاح القسم الثاني ما لا مال فيه أصلاً كالطلاق الخالي عن المال، القسم الثالث: ما كان المال فيه مقصوداً مثل الخلج والعتق على مال. ثم القسم الأول على ثلاثة أوجه الأول الهزل بأصله والثاني الهزل بقدر البدل الثالث الهزل في جنس البدل، ثم كل وجه من تلك الوجوه على أربعة أوجه بأن اتفقا على البناء أو على الإعراض أو سكتا، أو اختلفا فقال: وهذا إلخ. يجب الأقل: أي أقل المهر فيما هزلا به هذا شروع في القسم الأول، وهو ما كان المال فيه تبعاً كالنكاح، فإن المقصود الأصلي من الجانبين الحلّ الذي يحصل به التوالد والتناسل، والمال فيه لإظهار خطر المحل لا مقصوداً، فيكون تبعاً، وهذا نظير للهزل في قدر البدل وهو المهر، وصورةً بأن قال لها أو لوليّها: المهر في الواقع ألف، والتسمية عند الناس بألفين، ووافقه المرأة أو وليها على ذلك فالنكاح صحيح مطلقاً في الأحوال كلها، لكن في وجوب المسمّى أو ما تواضعا عليه تفصيل، وهو أنه إن اتفقا على الإعراض عن المواضعة بالهزل فاللازم هو المهر المسمّى، وهو ألفان بالاتفاق لبطلان المواضعة بالإعراض عنها ، أو اتفقا على البناء على المواضعة بالهزل فالمعتبر هو المواضعة بالهزل، ويكون المهر هو الألف الذي تواضعا عليه بالاتفاق أيضاً، وهذا ما بينه المصنف في المتـ وهذا بخلاف البيع حيث يجب الألفان عند أبي حنيفة به، وعندهما الألف قياساً على النكاح. ووجه الفرق هو أن قبول العقد في الألف الذي هزلا به شرط فاسد كما مرّ في البيع، فلا يمكن اعتباره في البيع؛ إذ هو يفسد بالشرط الفاسد بخلاف النكاح.
Chapter of Qiyas. Acquired attributes. With one hundred dinars on condition that the price is one thousand dirhams, then the jest is void and the stated (price) is valid in both cases according to Abu Hanifa. His two companions said: The sale is valid with one thousand dirhams in the first case, and with one hundred dinars in the second case, because it is possible to act upon the mutual understanding (muwada'a) regarding the price along with seriousness in the contract itself in the first case but not in the second. We (Hanafis) say that they are serious in the contract itself. [Section from Abu Hanifa's side]: Acting upon the mutual understanding regarding the substitute makes it a void condition in the sale, i.e., acceptance of part of the substitute. ... An example: with one hundred dinars: This is an analogy for jest in the genus of the consideration, and the stated (price) is valid, etc. The intended first case is jest in the amount of the price: they stated in the contract two thousand (dirhams) among the people, while the actual price is one thousand. In this scenario, the situation does not depart from four divisions: If they both ignore (i.e., agree to ignore the jest), the contract is valid and the price is the stated two thousand by consensus; if they both remain silent (i.e., do not consider the jest), or they differ regarding ignoring and building, then according to Abu Hanifa the stated price (two thousand) is considered, while his two companions consider the mutual understanding so the price is one thousand, and the one thousand they jested about becomes void; or if they both build (i.e., agree to build on the jest), then according to Abu Hanifa the stated is considered, while according to them the (actual) one thousand. This is what the author explained in the text. The intended second case is jest in the genus of the price: they mutually agreed to state among the people one hundred dinars, while the actual price is one thousand dirhams. The sale is valid and the price is the stated one hundred dinars by consensus in all four states. [Then discussion about the difference between the two cases, arguments of Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa's response, and comparison with marriage.]
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of the rulings on jest (hazl) in the price of a sale contract, specifically distinguishing between jest in the amount (qadr) and jest in the genus (jins) of the price. The author first presents the case where the parties jest about the amount: they agree that the actual price is 1000 but state 2000 in public. Abu Hanifa holds that in all four possible scenarios (agree to ignore, remain silent, differ, or agree to build on the jest), the stated price (2000) is the effective price unless they both agree to ignore the jest, in which case it is 2000 by consensus. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ: they consider the mutual understanding (muwada'a) about the actual price, so the price is 1000 except when they ignore the jest. The reasoning is that it is possible to combine seriousness in the contract with jest in the amount of the price, so the contract can be valid for 1000 and the extra 1000 is a void condition. However, Abu Hanifa argues that this extra amount is a void condition that invalidates the sale because it is a condition that is not part of the contract's requirements; unlike in marriage, a void condition does not invalidate the marriage but does invalidate a sale. In the second case (jest in the genus of the price: actual 1000 dirhams, stated 100 dinars), all agree that the sale is valid and the price is the stated 100 dinars, because it is impossible to combine seriousness in the contract with jest that negates the price entirely (since the stated amount is not a valid price in the given context). The passage then compares sale to marriage (nikah), where the consideration (mahr) is secondary; jest in the mahr does not invalidate the marriage, and the actual mahr is paid by agreement. This difference explains why the companions analogize the sale to marriage but Abu Hanifa rejects it.

Key Terms
الهزل (al-hazl): Jest or mockery; when parties utter a contract or term without serious intent.
المواضعة (al-muwada'a): Mutual agreement to be jesting; the hidden understanding that the stated terms are not binding.
التسمية (al-tasmiya): The stated price or consideration in the contract.
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is invalid and, in a sale, renders the contract void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The sale is void because the jest creates a void condition.

Key Takeaway
Jest in the amount of the sale price introduces a void condition that, according to Abu Hanifa, invalidates the sale unless the parties expressly ignore it; the Sahibayn allow the sale to stand with the actual price, drawing a key distinction between amount and genus.

The Hanafi Position on the Waw: Absolute Conjunction without Sequence or Simultaneity
Defines the waw as conjunction letter for absolute combination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule regarding the conjunction waw and analyze the dispute with those who claim it implies sequence.

Core Idea
The waw indicates mere sharing; sequence requires external evidence.

This lesson examines the foundational usul principle that the conjunction waw (و) indicates absolute combination (jam‘ mutlaq) without specifying sequence or simultaneity. Understanding this principle affects how we read many legal texts where multiple obligations or acts are joined by waw. The passage from the Usul text clarifies the Hanafi stance and contrasts it with opposing views, using the famous example of the sa‘i between Safa and Marwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Linguistic Claim
What does the Hanafi school say about the meaning of the conjunction waw? The passage states: 'wa hiya li mutlaq al-jam‘i ‘indana' – it is for absolute combination.
2
Locate the Key Principle
Why is waw considered the original (asl) among conjunction letters? Because it conveys mere sharing (mujarrad al-ishtirak), unlike other letters that add extra meaning such as sequence (thumma) or simultaneity (fa').
3
Examine the Opposing View
Which school argues that waw implies sequence, and what is their evidence? Some Shafi'i scholars cite the Prophet's action of beginning with Safa and his instruction 'Nabda’u bima bada’a Allah bihi' (We begin with what Allah began with), along with the verse 'Inna as-Safa wal-Marwata min sha‘a’iri Allah'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
How does the Hanafi school refute the argument from the hadith? If the waw itself implied sequence, the Prophet's instruction would be redundant. The order to start with Safa proves the order is external, not from the waw.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)? In the sa‘i, Hanafi holds that starting with Safa is sunnah, not wajib from the waw, while the opposing view may consider sequence required by the waw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حروف المعاني حروف العطف فشطر من مسائل الفقه مبنيّ عليها. وأكثرها وقوعاً حروف العطف، والأصل فيه الواو، أي الحروف أي العطف وهي لمطلق الجمع عندنا من غير تعرّض لمقارنة ولا ترتيب، وعليه عامة أهل اللغة باب حروف المعاني ولما كان هذا البحث من مسائل النحو إلا أنه يتعلق به بعض أحكام الشرع أورده في آخر الكتاب تتميماً للفائدة، وبعضهم كصاحب "المنار" الحق هذا البحث بالحقيقة والمجاز، وبالجملة هذا البحث من مبادي اللغوية، فحقه أن يذكر قبل المقاصد لكن المصنف لله ومن سلك مسلكه لم يراعوا الترتيب بين المبادئ والمقاصد، بل خلطوا بين مقاصد الفن ومباديه حروف المعانى احترز عن حروف المباني: وهي الحروف الهجاء الموضوعة لغرض التركيب لا للمعنى، والمراد بحروف المعاني ما توصل معاني الأفعال إلى الأسماء، أو ما تدلّ على معنى في غيره، ثم إطلاق الحروف على ذكر في هذا الباب تغليب؛ لأن كلمات الشروط والظروف المذكورة في هذا الباب أسماء. فشطر إلخ والشطر النصف والمراد به البعض فهذا تعليل لقوله: والذي يقع به ختم الكتاب حروف المعاني؛ لأن الكتاب في أصول الفقه، ما وهي يبتني عليه مسائل الفقه، والحروف أيضا تبتني عليها بعض المسائل، فوجب إدراج مبحثها في الكتاب ولكن لما كان من مسائل النحو الصرفة أورده في آخر الكتاب، فتأمل. وقوعاً: في الكلام واستعمالاً فيه. حروف العطف لأنها تدخل على الأفعال والأسماء بخلاف حروف الجر وكلمات الشرط، فإن الأولى لاتدخل على الأفعال، والثانية لاتدخل على الأسماء والعطف في اللغة الثني ،والردّ وفي الاصطلاح أن يرد أحل المفردين إلى الآخر فيما حكمت أو إحدى الجملتين إلى الأخرى في الحصول، وفائدته الاختصار وإثبات المشاركة، كذا قيل. الواو : لأن سائر الحروف تدل على معنى زائد على الاشتراك بخلاف الواو فإنها لمجرد الاشتراك، فهي بمنزلة المطلق، وسائر الحروف بمنزلة المقيّد، و المطلق أولى بالأصالة. لمقارنة: أي معية في الزمان كما ذهب إليه بعض أصحابنا ولا ترتيب أي تقدّم أحدهما على الآخر في الزمان كما ذهب إليه بعض أصحاب الشافعي، مستدلاً بقوله عليه السلام نبدأ بما بدأ الله به، فبدأ بالصفا، وقرأ إن الصفا والمروة من شعائر الله). رواه الترمذي وأبو داؤد والمالك في مؤطائه [الترمذي رقم: ٨٦٢] ففهم عليها منه الترتيب * ، * الترتيب وقد أجيب عنه أنه لو كان الترتيب يفهم من الآية لما قال عليه السلام: "ابدؤوا بما بدأ الله تعالى به". رواه النسائي والدار قطني بصيغة الأمر.
Chapter of Particles of Meanings: Conjunction letters. A portion of fiqh issues is based on them. The most frequent in occurrence are the conjunction letters, and the original among them is the waw. That is, the letters, that is, conjunction. And it (the waw) is for absolute combination according to us, without indicating simultaneity or sequence. The majority of linguists agree... This chapter of particles of meanings distinguishes from letters of construction (huruf al-mabani) which are the alphabet letters. The intended meaning of huruf al-ma'ani is what connects meanings of verbs to nouns, or what indicates a meaning in something else. Then the term 'letters' here is used predominately because words of conditions and adverbs in this chapter are nouns. ... The waw is the original because other letters indicate an additional meaning beyond the sharing, unlike the waw which is for mere sharing, so it is like the absolute, and other letters are like the restricted, and the absolute is more original. Regarding 'muqarana' (simultaneity): some of our companions hold it indicates simultaneity in time; and 'no sequence' means no precedence of one over the other, as some Shafi'i companions hold, using as evidence his statement (peace be upon him): 'We begin with what Allah began with,' so he began with Safa, and recited: 'Indeed, Safa and Marwa are among the symbols of Allah.' [Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Malik in Muwatta] They understood sequence from this. The response is that if sequence were understood from the verse, he would not have said: 'Begin with what Allah began with.' Narrated by Nasa'i and Dar Qutni in imperative form.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on particles of meanings (huruf al-ma'ani), focusing on conjunction letters (huruf al-‘atf). It explains that these are important for fiqh because many rulings depend on conjunction. The primary letter is waw, which in the Hanafi school indicates absolute combination (jam‘ mutlaq) without implying simultaneity (muqarana) or sequence (tartib). The majority of linguists agree with this view. The text then distinguishes huruf al-ma'ani from huruf al-mabani (alphabet letters). The inclusion of this grammatical discussion in a usul al-fiqh work is justified because many fiqh rules are built on conjunction. The waw is considered the original (asl) because it conveys mere participation, unlike other conjunction letters that add extra meaning. The passage also addresses a dispute: some Shafi‘i scholars argue that waw implies sequence, citing the hadith where the Prophet began with Safa and said 'Nabda’u bima bada’a Allah bihi' (We begin with what Allah began with), and the verse 'Inna as-Safa wal-Marwata min sha‘a’iri Allah.' The Hanafi response is that if the verse itself implied sequence, the Prophet would not have needed to give the order to begin with what Allah began; rather the order itself shows that the waw alone does not indicate sequence. The imperative to begin with what Allah began proves that the order is additional, not from the conjunction.

Key Terms
حروف المعاني (ḥurūf al-ma‘ānī): Particles that convey meanings, connecting verbs to nouns or indicating a meaning in something else.
الواو (al-wāw): The conjunction letter waw, which for Hanafi indicates absolute combination without sequence or simultaneity.
مطلق الجمع (muṭlaq al-jam‘): Absolute combination, indicating that the conjuncts are joined without any specification of time order or simultaneity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what does the conjunction waw indicate?
A) Sequence (tartib) only.
B) Simultaneity (muqarana) only.
C) Absolute combination without sequence or simultaneity.
D) Both simultaneity and sequence together.

Key Takeaway
The conjunction waw in legal texts does not by itself indicate sequence or simultaneity; it merely joins elements, and any order must come from independent evidence.

The Default Ruling of the Particle Fa – Immediate Sequence
Textual analysis of the particle fa's primary function

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default function of the particle fa in Hanafi usul and apply it to conditional legal utterances to determine whether a condition is fulfilled.

Core Idea
Fa indicates that the second action must follow the first immediately, without any delay.

In Hanafi usul, the meaning of particles is foundational for interpreting legal language. The particle fa primarily signifies immediate sequence. This lesson focuses on that default meaning through a clear example from conditional divorce. Understanding this rule will help you analyze similar conditional statements in contracts and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default meaning of fa
The author states that الفاء is for connection (وصل) and immediate sequence (تعقيب). This is the default ruling: when fa joins two actions, the second follows without delay.
This is a linguistic rule accepted by Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the divorce example
Consider the statement: 'If you enter this house, then this house, you are divorced.' The fa after 'then' requires that the second entry occurs immediately after the first. If she delays, the condition fails.
The object of 'we said' in the Arabic text indicates the condition for divorce.
3
Apply the rule to determine the ruling
If she enters the second house after a delay, the condition is not met, so divorce does not occur. If she enters the second house immediately after the first, the condition is fulfilled and divorce takes effect.
The ruling is derived from the literal meaning of fa.
4
Note the exception (preview)
The passage also mentions an exception: when fa enters on a continuous cause, it can indicate delay. This will be covered in a separate lesson, but be aware that the default rule has limits.

Among them is that his saying 'you are free' and 'you are safe' are from the estimated circumstances, like His saying exalted: ﴿then enter it forever﴾ (Az-Zumar 39:73) meaning estimating eternity, not from actual circumstances. So its meaning is 'Give me a thousand dirhams while you are estimating that freedom is at the moment of payment, and descend while you are estimating that safety is at the moment of descending.' And since the speaker affirmed freedom and safety in the states of payment and descent, they are attached to them, non-existent at present, so their precedence over them is not necessary; rather precedence is for the estimation, and there is no harm in it. Among them is that the circumstantial sentence stands in place of the answer to the command, as if it was said: 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you will become free, and descend and you will become safe.' So freedom is attached to payment and safety to descent, so they do not precede them. Among them is that freedom and safety are states of payment and descent, and the state is an attribute, and the attribute does not precede the described, so freedom and safety do not precede payment and descent. For connection and immediate sequence, i.e., that the coordinated is connected to the coordinate with immediate sequence without delay. We said: the object of 'we said' is his saying: the condition: for the occurrence of divorce without delay; if she does not enter the two houses, or enters only one of them, or enters the first after the second, or enters the second after the first with delay, the divorce occurs due to the loss of the condition. On causes: although the original is that it enters on rulings; because the ruling is consequent upon a cause, so immediate sequence is realized, and it does not enter on the causes; because the cause is not delayed from its effect but rather precedes it, so where is immediate sequence? Except that it may enter on causes contrary to the original. In the sense of delay: because when the cause is perpetual in existence, it is in the state of perpetuity delayed from the beginning of the existence of the ruling, so immediate sequence is realized by this consideration, so the entry of fa upon them is correct, as it is said to one who is in the prison of a ruler: 'Rejoice, for relief has come.' So relief is the cause for rejoicing, but it remains after the beginning of rejoicing, so immediate sequence occurs, so the entry of fa upon it is correct, and this fa is called fa of causation; because it is in the meaning of lam of causation. I say there is a consideration in it; because the cause for rejoicing is the arrival of relief, and it is [؟] that it does not remain for a time, but as for the relief that remains, it is not a cause for it. So reflect. And for this, i.e., because fa may enter on a perpetual cause.
* Reflect: I say: There is an indication to the answer to the consideration: that the occurrence of the arrival of relief is [؟] coming, except that its remaining is not coming but rather temporal. (Abu Turab Muhammad Abdul Haqq)
[PAGE_340]
Chapter on particles of meanings
He is freed immediately; because manumission is perpetual and resembles the delayed, and as for perpetuity, it is where it remains to a period.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the particle fa (الفاء) in legal utterances. The author begins by stating the default rule: الفاء indicates connection (وصل) and immediate sequence (تعقيب), meaning that the second action must follow the first without any delay. He illustrates this with an example: if a man tells his wife 'If you enter this house, then this house, you are divorced,' the condition is that she enters the second house immediately after the first. If she delays, the condition fails and divorce does not occur. Then the author discusses an exception: الفاء can enter on a cause (علة) when that cause is perpetual (دائم), and in that case it acquires the meaning of delay (تراخي). He gives the example of saying 'Rejoice, for relief has come' – here, الفاء enters on the cause (relief) even though relief precedes rejoicing, but because relief continues, it is as if it is delayed relative to the rejoicing. He then applies this to the legal phrasing: 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you are free' (أد إلي ألفاً فأنت حر). The author explores three interpretations to avoid the conclusion that freedom precedes the giving. First, he suggests that 'you are free' is an estimated circumstantial clause (حال مقدّرة), not an actual state – like the Quranic verse 'enter it forever' where 'forever' is an estimated state. Thus the meaning is 'give while you are estimating that you will be free at the moment of giving.' Second, the circumstantial clause stands for the answer to the command, so freedom is attached to the giving and does not precede it. Third, freedom is a state of the giving; as an attribute, it cannot precede its subject. The author then explains the original rule that الفاء should only enter on rulings (أحكام), not on causes, because the cause precedes the ruling. But it may enter on a perpetual cause, such as continuous relief, giving the sense of delay. He notes a criticism: the cause for rejoicing is the arrival of relief, which is instantaneous, not perpetual. A footnote offers a response: the arrival is an event, but its continued effect can be considered as if it remains over time. Finally, the passage applies the rule to manumission: since manumission is perpetual, it resembles the delayed, so the slave is freed immediately upon the statement.

Key Terms
الفاء (al-faa): A particle of conjunction primarily indicating immediate sequence (تعقيب) between two actions.
التعقيب (al-ta'qeeb): Immediate succession without delay; the second action follows the first without any intervening time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default meaning of the particle fa as stated in the passage?
A) It indicates a cause and effect relationship.
B) It indicates immediate sequence without delay.
C) It indicates simultaneity of two actions.
D) It indicates a possibility of delay.

Key Takeaway
The default ruling of الفاء is immediate sequence; any delay violates the condition.

Exceptional Use of Fa with Continuous Causes – Delay
Textual analysis of the exceptional use of fa with continuous causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when الفاء can indicate delay due to a continuous cause and apply the three Hanafi interpretations to prevent legal contradictions.

Core Idea
When fa enters on a continuous cause, it indicates delay, not immediate sequence.

The default rule of fa is immediate sequence, but the passage introduces an important exception: when fa is attached to a cause (علة) that is perpetual in existence, it takes the meaning of delay. This is crucial for understanding statements like 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you are free,' where the freedom should not precede the giving. The passage provides three linguistic arguments to resolve this apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the exception scenario
The author states that fa can enter on a cause (like 'relief has come' in 'Rejoice, for relief has come') when the cause is continuous. In such cases, fa indicates delay because the cause persists.
The example: 'أبشر فقد أتاك الغوث' – relief is a continuous cause.
2
Analyze the manumission statement
Consider 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you are free.' If fa indicated immediate sequence, freedom would follow the giving. But the speaker intends freedom to be conditional on giving; it should not precede. The author offers three interpretations to avoid this.
The three interpretations are numbered 'منها' in the Arabic.
3
Understand the first interpretation – estimated state
'You are free' is an estimated circumstantial clause (حال مقدّرة), like 'forever' in the Quran. The meaning is 'Give while you are estimating that you will be free at the moment of giving.' The freedom is estimated, not actual, at the time of speech.
Proof: Quran 39:73: 'Enter it forever' – 'forever' is an estimated state.
4
Understand the second interpretation – circumstantial clause as answer
The circumstantial clause 'you are free' stands in place of the answer to the command. It is as if he said 'Give and you will become free.' So freedom is attached to the giving, not preceding it.
This treats 'fate free' as the result of the command.
5
Understand the third interpretation – attribute does not precede its subject
Freedom is a state (حال) of the giving, like an attribute. An attribute cannot precede its described subject, so freedom cannot precede the giving. Thus, the fa does not imply that freedom occurs before giving.
This is a grammatical argument based on word order.

Among them is that his saying 'you are free' and 'you are safe' are from the estimated circumstances, like His saying exalted: ﴿then enter it forever﴾ (Az-Zumar 39:73) meaning estimating eternity, not from actual circumstances. So its meaning is 'Give me a thousand dirhams while you are estimating that freedom is at the moment of payment, and descend while you are estimating that safety is at the moment of descending.' And since the speaker affirmed freedom and safety in the states of payment and descent, they are attached to them, non-existent at present, so their precedence over them is not necessary; rather precedence is for the estimation, and there is no harm in it. Among them is that the circumstantial sentence stands in place of the answer to the command, as if it was said: 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you will become free, and descend and you will become safe.' So freedom is attached to payment and safety to descent, so they do not precede them. Among them is that freedom and safety are states of payment and descent, and the state is an attribute, and the attribute does not precede the described, so freedom and safety do not precede payment and descent. For connection and immediate sequence, i.e., that the coordinated is connected to the coordinate with immediate sequence without delay. We said: the object of 'we said' is his saying: the condition: for the occurrence of divorce without delay; if she does not enter the two houses, or enters only one of them, or enters the first after the second, or enters the second after the first with delay, the divorce occurs due to the loss of the condition. On causes: although the original is that it enters on rulings; because the ruling is consequent upon a cause, so immediate sequence is realized, and it does not enter on the causes; because the cause is not delayed from its effect but rather precedes it, so where is immediate sequence? Except that it may enter on causes contrary to the original. In the sense of delay: because when the cause is perpetual in existence, it is in the state of perpetuity delayed from the beginning of the existence of the ruling, so immediate sequence is realized by this consideration, so the entry of fa upon them is correct, as it is said to one who is in the prison of a ruler: 'Rejoice, for relief has come.' So relief is the cause for rejoicing, but it remains after the beginning of rejoicing, so immediate sequence occurs, so the entry of fa upon it is correct, and this fa is called fa of causation; because it is in the meaning of lam of causation. I say there is a consideration in it; because the cause for rejoicing is the arrival of relief, and it is [؟] that it does not remain for a time, but as for the relief that remains, it is not a cause for it. So reflect. And for this, i.e., because fa may enter on a perpetual cause.
* Reflect: I say: There is an indication to the answer to the consideration: that the occurrence of the arrival of relief is [؟] coming, except that its remaining is not coming but rather temporal. (Abu Turab Muhammad Abdul Haqq)
[PAGE_340]
Chapter on particles of meanings
He is freed immediately; because manumission is perpetual and resembles the delayed, and as for perpetuity, it is where it remains to a period.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the particle fa (الفاء) in legal utterances. The author begins by stating the default rule: الفاء indicates connection (وصل) and immediate sequence (تعقيب), meaning that the second action must follow the first without any delay. He illustrates this with an example: if a man tells his wife 'If you enter this house, then this house, you are divorced,' the condition is that she enters the second house immediately after the first. If she delays, the condition fails and divorce does not occur. Then the author discusses an exception: الفاء can enter on a cause (علة) when that cause is perpetual (دائم), and in that case it acquires the meaning of delay (تراخي). He gives the example of saying 'Rejoice, for relief has come' – here, الفاء enters on the cause (relief) even though relief precedes rejoicing, but because relief continues, it is as if it is delayed relative to the rejoicing. He then applies this to the legal phrasing: 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you are free' (أد إلي ألفاً فأنت حر). The author explores three interpretations to avoid the conclusion that freedom precedes the giving. First, he suggests that 'you are free' is an estimated circumstantial clause (حال مقدّرة), not an actual state – like the Quranic verse 'enter it forever' where 'forever' is an estimated state. Thus the meaning is 'give while you are estimating that you will be free at the moment of giving.' Second, the circumstantial clause stands for the answer to the command, so freedom is attached to the giving and does not precede it. Third, freedom is a state of the giving; as an attribute, it cannot precede its subject. The author then explains the original rule that الفاء should only enter on rulings (أحكام), not on causes, because the cause precedes the ruling. But it may enter on a perpetual cause, such as continuous relief, giving the sense of delay. He notes a criticism: the cause for rejoicing is the arrival of relief, which is instantaneous, not perpetual. A footnote offers a response: the arrival is an event, but its continued effect can be considered as if it remains over time. Finally, the passage applies the rule to manumission: since manumission is perpetual, it resembles the delayed, so the slave is freed immediately upon the statement.

Key Terms
التعقيب (al-ta'qeeb): Immediate succession without delay.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): Delay; the opposite of immediate sequence.
الحال المقدّرة (al-haal al-muqaddara): An estimated circumstantial clause that expresses a state not actually present but intended by the speaker.
فاء التعليل (fā' al-ta'līl): The fa of causation, which is like the lam of causation, indicating a cause-effect relationship with delayed sequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The passage provides three interpretations to prevent freedom from preceding the giving in 'Give me a thousand dirhams and you are free.' Which of the following is NOT one of them?
A) 'You are free' is an estimated circumstantial clause.
B) The circumstantial clause stands as the answer to the command.
C) Freedom is an attribute that cannot precede its subject.
D) The fa indicates that freedom is granted immediately upon the statement.

Key Takeaway
When fa enters on a continuous cause, it indicates delay, and estimated circumstantial clauses preserve the intended conditionality.

The Particle 'Lakinna' for Istidrak After Negation
Defining 'lakinna' as a particle for istidrak after negation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of 'lakinna' as a particle for istidrak after negation and apply it to identify correction in negated statements.

Core Idea
'Lakinna' corrects a misunderstanding that the negation applies to the next item.

This lesson introduces you to a crucial particle in Hanafi usul: 'lakinna'. Unlike ordinary 'but', 'lakinna' has a specific function: it corrects a potential misunderstanding that arises from a preceding negation. Mastering this definition will help you read Arabic legal texts more accurately and understand how scholars derive rulings from the nuances of language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its context
Read the Arabic text and locate the word 'لكن'. Then check what comes before it: is it a negated statement (khabar manfi)?
In the source example, 'ما جاءني زيد' is a negated statement before 'لكن'.
2
Understand istidrak
Istidrak means 'correction'. The speaker uses 'lakinna' to correct the listener's assumption that the negation covers the next item. So after negation, 'lakinna' affirms the following item.
This is different from ordinary contrast; it specifically targets a misunderstanding.
3
Distinguish from 'bal'
The source contrasts 'lakinna' with 'bal'. 'Bal' can also correct, but it is used after affirmatives or in performative statements as a pure conjunctive. 'Lakinna' is only for negation.
In divorce examples, 'bal' cannot retract a performative, so it acts as a simple conjunctive.
4
Apply the definition to a new example
Given a sentence like 'لم يقرأ زيد لكن عمرو' (Zaid did not read but Amr did), explain that 'lakinna' corrects the assumption that Amr also did not read.
This shows how the particle functions in actual analysis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
["لكن" وحكمها]
الكلام
وأما "لكن فللاستدراك بعد النفي، تقول: ما جاءني زيد
= زيد؛ إذ هو لم يكن مقصوداً لنا، وإنما المقصود إثبات المجيئ لعمرو، فزيد يحتمل مجيئه وعدمه، لا أن مجيئ زيد باطــــل وخطأ في الواقع، وهذا معنى الغلط وتداركه هذا هو مذهب المحققين، وقيل: معنى الإعراض الرجوع عن الأول وإبطاله. ف واعلم أن الإعراض عما قبله إنما يصح إذا كان ما قبله صالحاً للإعراض كما في الأخبار، فإن كان لا يحتمل ذلك كما في الإنشاءات فتصير كلمة "بل" للعطف المحض، فتعمل في إثبات الثاني مضموماً إلى الأول على سبيل الجمع دون الترتيب ولذا قالوا إلخ. إنه يقع الثلاث إلخ لأن قوله إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق واحدة" إنشاء لا يحتمل الرجوع عنه بكلمة بل، فيقع ما قبل "بل" وما بعدها على سبيل الجمع عند وجود الشرط بغير ترتيب، وإنما قيد بقوله "قبل الدخول بها" ليصح الفرق الذي بينه بقوله: بخلاف العطف بالواو عند أبي حنيفة وحليه حيث لا يقع إلا واحدة فيما إذا قال لها: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق واحدة وثنتين؛ لأن قوله "وثنتين" معطوف على قوله فأنت طالق واحدة"، فيتعلّق بالشرط بواسطة والأول بغير واسطة، والواسطة يقدم على ما هو واسطة له، فعند وجود الشرط ينزل على الترتيب، فيقع الأول أولاً، فإذا وقع لم يبق المحل للآخرين؛ لأنها غير موطوءة. نعم لو كان موطوءة لوقع الكل، وأما عندهما فيقع الكل لاشتراكهما في الشرط، وقد مر تشريحه فتذكر. لأنه : دليل على وقوع الثلاث بلا واسطة لإبطال المعطوف عليه وإقامة المعطوف مقامه ولذا قال: لكن بشرط إلخ. إبطال الأول: إذ لو لم يبطل الأول وهو المعطوف عليه لا تصل الثاني أي المعطوف بالشرط بواسطة. ذلك: الإبطال؛ لأنه تعلق بالشرط على سبيل اللزوم. بغير واسطة فيجعل كأن الشرط ثبت هنا مذكوراً، لا أنه حذف اختصاراً، فيتعلق الطلقتان بالشرط بلا واسطة الحلف بيمينين بأن قال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق واحدة، ثم قال: إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثنيتن، فإذا دخلت مرة واحدة يقع الثلاث ما في وسعه وهو إفراد الثاني بالشرط، ولا يثبت ما ليس في وسعه وهو إبطال الأول، فيقع الثلاث كما قررنا لك.

['Lakinna' and its ruling] Speech. As for 'lakinna', it is for istidrak (correction) after negation. You say: 'Zaid did not come to me' = Zaid; because he was not our intention, rather the intention is to affirm coming for 'Amr. So Zaid's coming is possible and its opposite, not that Zaid's coming is false and an error in reality. This is the meaning of error and its correction. This is the way of the verifiers. And it is said: the meaning of turning away is returning from the first and annulling it. Know that turning away from what is before is only valid if what is before is susceptible to turning away, as in informative statements. If it is not susceptible, as in performatives, then 'bal' becomes a pure conjunctive, so it acts in affirming the second added to the first in the manner of combination without order, and therefore they said etc. That three occur etc. Because his saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once' is a performative that cannot be abrogated by 'bal', so what is before 'bal' and what is after it occur in combination upon the existence of the condition without order. And he restricted it with 'before consummation' to make correct the difference he made between his saying 'unlike the conjunction with waw according to Abu Hanifa and his two' where only one occurs when he says to her 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once and twice' because his saying 'and twice' is conjoined to his saying 'you are divorced once', so it is attached to the condition by means of an intermediary and the first without intermediary, and the intermediary is advanced over that which is a means for it; thus when the condition exists, it is placed in order, so the first occurs first, and when it occurs, there remains no place for the others because she is not consummated. Yes, if she were consummated, all would occur. But according to the two, all occur because of their sharing in the condition, and their analysis has passed, so remember. Because it is evidence for the occurrence of three without an intermediary for cancellation of the conjoined and setting up the conjoining in its place. Therefore he said: but with the condition of annulling the first. Annulling the first: because if the first (the conjoined) is not annulled, the second (the conjoined) does not attach to the condition by means of an intermediary. That: the annulment; because it is attached to the condition in a necessary manner. Without an intermediary it makes it as if the condition is mentioned here, not that it is omitted for brevity, so the two divorces attach to the condition without an intermediary like swearing two oaths: by saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced once' then saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced twice', so when she enters once, three occur, which is within his capacity: to isolate the second by the condition; and what is not within his capacity does not occur, i.e., annulling the first. So three occur as we have explained to you.
After negation: i.e., to remove a misunderstanding arising from the previous negated speech. 'Zaid did not come to me' might create the impression that 'Amr also did not come due to similarity.

Commentary
This passage defines the particle 'lakinna' (but, however) as a particle for istidrak (correction) used specifically after a negated statement. For example, if you say 'Zaid did not come to me but 'Amr', the purpose is to correct the potential misunderstanding that 'Amr also did not come. The author contrasts this with 'bal' (rather) which is used to correct an error in affirmative statements or to function as a pure conjunctive in performatives. The text then goes into a detailed discussion of the divorce case that was already presented in the previous lesson, but here it is used to illustrate the difference between 'lakinna' and 'bal'. The author notes that in performative utterances like the divorce statement, 'bal' acts as a pure conjunctive, not as a corrector of error. The passage also revisits the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the use of 'waw'. This shows how different particles lead to different legal outcomes. The commentary here should focus on the definition of 'lakinna' and its distinction from 'bal'.

Key Terms
استدراك (istidrak): Correction of a misunderstanding that could arise from a preceding negated statement.
نفي (nafy): Negation; a statement that denies something.
لكن (lākinna): A particle used for istidrak after negation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
'Lakinna' is a particle exclusive to correcting misunderstandings that arise after negated statements, affirming the item that follows.

The Hanafi Analysis of 'Aw' (أو) in Reports and Performatives
Explaining the rulings of 'aw' for doubt in reports and choice in commands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the meanings of 'aw' (أو) in report (khabar) and performative (insha') contexts, apply the Hanafi principle that 'aw' indicates one of two without specification, and evaluate the opposing view that 'aw' indicates doubt.

Core Idea
أو لأحد المذكورين غير عين — الشك والتخيير من السياق لا من الوضع.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on the conjunction particle 'aw' (or). The core debate is whether 'aw' inherently means doubt or choice, or whether these meanings derive from the context of speech. The Hanafi school, following the majority of linguists and usul scholars, holds that 'aw' simply indicates one of two things without specification (لأحد المذكورين غير عين). In reports, the lack of specification leads to doubt; in performatives (commands, declarations), it necessitates choice. This distinction has significant legal implications, as seen in the example of emancipating one of two slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic function of 'aw'
State the Hanafi position: 'aw' indicates one of the two mentioned without specifying which. Note that it does not inherently mean doubt or choice.
2
Distinguish between report (khabar) and performative (insha')
When 'aw' enters a report, the lack of specification leads to doubt about which one occurred. When it enters a performative (command, declaration), it gives the doer a choice.
The doubt or choice is external — from the context, not from the particle itself.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Analyze Quran 4:66: 'Kill yourselves or leave your homes.' Here 'aw' is in a command (performative) and indicates a choice between the two actions.
The Hanafi interpretation: the verse gives a choice, not doubt.
4
Evaluate the opposing view
Some scholars (Qadi Abu Zaid, Abu Ishaq al-Isfaraini) argue that 'aw' is for doubt. The Hanafi response: if it were for doubt, then in commands it would create doubt, which is impossible because commands require clear direction. Therefore, the particle itself is neutral; the doubt arises from the context of uncertain reports.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in usul al-fiqh.
5
Apply to a legal example
Consider someone saying 'This is free or this' regarding two slaves. If the statement is a performative (إنشاء), 'aw' gives choice — the owner may free either. If it is a report (خبر), it clarifies that one was already free.
The practical consequence: the ruling depends on whether the statement is considered inceptive or reportative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حروف المعاني
حروف العطف
[ "أو" وحكمها ]
وأما "أو " فتدخل بين اسمين أو فعلين فيتناول أحد المذكورين، فإن دخلت في الخبر أفضت إلى الشك، وإن دخلت في الابتداء والإنشاء أوجبت التخيير. ولهذا قلنا فيمن قال: هذا حر أو هذا، إنه لما كان انشاء يحتمل الخبر أوجبت التخيير على كلمة "أو " احتمال أنه بيان حتى جعل البيان إنشاءاً من وجه إظهاراً من وجه، القيد فقط، فاندفع ما قال صاحب "غاية التحقيق": من أن في تلك الصورة أيضاً لايتسق الكلام؛ لأنه نفي فعل وإثباته بعينه فتأمل أحد المذكورين ففي المفردين تفيد ثبوت الحكم لأحدهما، كقولك: جاءني زيد أو بكر، أو بأحدهما كما تقول زيد قاعد أو قائم وفي الجملتين تفيد حصول مضمون أحدهما، كقوله تعالى: أَنِ اقْتُلُوا أَنْفُسَكُمْ أَوِ اخْرُجُوا مِنْ دِيَارِكُمْ (النساء: ٦٦). هذا هو مذهب عامة أهل اللغة وأئمة الأصول، وذهب القاضي الإمام أبو زيد وأبو اسحق الإسفرائي وجماعة من النحويين إلى أن كلمة "أو " للشك، وهذا ليس بسديد؛ لأن الشك باعتبار محل الكلام وإليه أشار أفضت إلى الشك باعتبار محل الكلام، لا أنها وضعت للشك، كما في قولك جاءني زيد أو خالد كان المقصود هو الإخبار عن مجيئ أحدهما لكن بغير تعين، فوقع الشك بهذا الاعتبار لا أنها موضوعة له في الابتداء كما في قولك: اضرب هذا أو هذا. والإنشاء: كقولك: هذا حرّ أو هذا أوجبت التخيير لأن الشك الذي كان ينشأ من محل الكلام لا يوجد هنا؛ لأنه لإثبات الحكم ابتداء، فيعود إلى أصله وهو التناول لأحدهما من غير تعين والأمر في الابتداء للايتمار، وهو لا يثبت بإيقاع الفعل في غير العين؛ لأن المأمور لا يعلم مراد الأمر، فثبت ضرورة التمكن من الايتمار، وكذا في الإنشاء لما تناول أحدهما غير عين أو جبت التخيير لدفع الإبهام، فالحاصل كما أن الشك في الإخبار يثبت من خارج كذلك التخيير في الابتداء والإنشاء يثبت من خارج لا أنها موضوعة لهما. ولهذا: أي لأجل أن "أو" لأحد الشيئين غير عين، وإنما يثبت الشك والتخيير بمحل الكلام. لما كان إنشاء: شرعاً؛ لأن الشرع وضعه لإيجاد الحرية. يحتمل الخبر: لغة؛ لأن وضعه في اللغة للإخبار التخيير حتى يكون له ولاية إيقاع هذا العتق في أيهما شاء بيان للحرّية السابقة على هذا الكلام. انشاءا من وجه إلخ فكما المبين وهو قوله: "هذا حرّ أو هذا يحتمل الوجهين أي الإنشائية والخبرية، فمن حيث الإنشائية يوجب التخيير حتى التخيير حتى كان له أن يوقع العتق في أيهما شاء، ومن حيث الخبرية يحتمل البيان للخبر المجهول الصادر عنه، كذلك البيان، وهو التعين بأن يعين ويقول: هذا كان مرادا لي يحتمل الوجهين المذكورين،
Chapter on Particles of Meaning - Conjunction Particles. [The particle 'aw' and its ruling]. As for 'aw', it enters between two nouns or two verbs and applies to one of the two mentioned. If it enters into a report, it leads to doubt; if it enters into a beginning (inceptive) or a performative (insha'), it necessitates choice. For this reason we said regarding one who said: 'This is free or this', since it was a performative that can be interpreted as a report, it necessitated choice upon the word 'aw' with the possibility that it is an explanation, making the explanation a performative in one aspect and a showing in another aspect, only the restriction, thus rebutting what the author of 'Ghāyat al-Taḥqīq' said: that in that case also the speech is not coherent because it is negation of an act and affirmation of the same act. So reflect. One of the two mentioned: in the case of two singulars, it indicates the establishment of the ruling for one of them, like your saying: 'Zayd or Bakr came to me', or for one of them as you say 'Zayd is sitting or standing'. In the case of two sentences, it indicates the occurrence of the content of one of them, like the verse: 'Kill yourselves or leave your homes' (Quran 4:66). This is the doctrine of the generality of linguists and leading scholars of usul. Qadi Imam Abu Zaid and Abu Ishaq al-Isfaraini and a group of grammarians went that the word 'aw' is for doubt, but this is not sound; because doubt is due to the context of the speech, as he indicated 'it leads to doubt due to the context of the speech', not that it is placed for doubt, as in your saying 'Zayd or Khalid came to me' – the intended meaning was to inform of the coming of one of them but without specification, so doubt occurred by this consideration, not that it is placed for it in the beginning, as in your saying: 'Strike this or this'. And the performative: like your saying: 'This is free or this' necessitated choice because the doubt that arises from the context of speech does not exist here; because it is to establish a ruling from the beginning, so it returns to its original meaning which is applying to one of the two without specification. The command in the beginning is for compliance, and it is not established by executing the act on a non-specific object because the commanded person does not know the desire of the commander, so it is established necessarily to enable compliance. Similarly in the performative, when it applies to one of the two without specification, it necessitates choice to remove ambiguity. The conclusion is that just as doubt in reports is established externally, so too choice in inceptives and performatives is established externally, not that they are placed for them. For this reason: i.e., because 'aw' is for one of two things without specification, and doubt and choice are only established by the context of speech. Since it was a performative: according to Sharia; because Sharia placed it to create freedom. It can be a report: linguistically; because its linguistic placement is for informing, choice so that he has the authority to effect this emancipation in whichever he wishes, an explanation of the freedom preceding this speech. As a performative in one aspect etc. So just as the explained (mubayan) which is his statement: 'This is free or this' can bear two aspects, i.e., performative and reportative, so from the performative aspect it necessitates choice until choice until he has the ability to effect the emancipation in whichever he wishes, and from the reportative aspect it can be an explanation of the unknown report issued from him. Similarly, the explanation, which is specification by specifying and saying: 'This was intended by me', can bear the two mentioned aspects.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage analyzes the conjunction particle 'aw' (or). The core issue is whether 'aw' itself indicates doubt or choice, or whether these meanings arise from context. The majority of linguists and usul scholars hold that 'aw' simply indicates one of two things without specification (لأحد المذكورين غير عين). When used in a report (خبر) like 'Zayd or Bakr came', the lack of specification leads to doubt on the part of the listener, but the particle itself is not for doubt. When used in inceptive or performative contexts (ابتداء وإنشاء) like commands or declarations, it necessitates choice for the doer, e.g., 'Strike this or this' gives choice. The passage applies this to a legal example: someone says 'This slave is free or this' – this utterance can be either a performative creating freedom or a report explaining a previous unknown emancipation. If it is performative, 'aw' gives choice, so he can free either one. If it is a report, it clarifies that one of them was already free. The passage refutes the view of Qadi Abu Zaid and others that 'aw' is for doubt, showing that doubt and choice are contextual. It also mentions the ruling about negated restricted speech, referencing the 'Ghāyat al-Taḥqīq' discussion.

Key Terms
أو (aw): حرف عطف يفيد التناول لأحد المذكورين غير عين
الابتداء والإنشاء (al-ibtidā' wa al-inshā'): الكلام الذي ينشئ حكماً ابتداءً كالأمر والإيجاب
الخبر (al-khabar): الكلام الذي يحتمل الصدق والكذب، ويخبر عن شيء ماض أو حاضر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
إذا قال شخص: 'اضرب زيداً أو عمراً'، فما حكم 'أو' هنا؟
A) تفيد الشك في المأمور
B) تفيد التخيير للمأمور
C) تفيد الجمع بينهما
D) لا تفيد شيئاً

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' does not inherently mean doubt or choice; its function is to indicate one of two without specification, and the context of speech (report or performative) determines whether doubt or choice arises.

The Particle 'Aw' in Hanafi Usul: Meaning, Context, and Legal Implications
Analyzing the particle 'aw' for doubt, choice, generality, and metaphor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on the particle 'aw' and apply it to distinguish doubt (shakk) from choice (takhyir) in legal contexts.

Core Idea
The particle 'aw' denotes one of two unspecified items; doubt and choice are contextual effects, not inherent meanings.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi usul analysis of the Arabic particle 'أو' (aw). While commonly understood as 'or', its legal meaning varies based on context: in reports it creates doubt about which event occurred, while in performatives (like vows) it gives the agent a choice. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting oaths, vows, and other legal speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic meaning of 'aw'
State the foundational Hanafi position: 'aw' indicates one of two or more things without specifying which. This is the default meaning, derived from linguistic usage and Quranic evidence.
The text emphasizes that 'aw' is not inherently for doubt or choice.
2
Distinguish between khabar and insha' contexts
Classify the utterance as either a report (khabar) or a performative (insha'). Reports describe an event; performatives create a new legal state (e.g., vows, freeing slaves).
This classification determines whether 'aw' yields doubt or choice.
3
Explain why doubt arises in reports
In reports, the speaker mentions two possibilities but does not specify which occurred. The listener experiences doubt because of this lack of specification. The doubt is a consequence of the context, not the particle itself.
Example: 'Zayd or Khalid came to me.'
4
Explain why choice arises in performatives
In performatives, the speaker uses 'aw' to offer alternatives without specifying which to take. Since the agent must comply, 'aw' gives a choice to select one option. No doubt arises because the ruling is being established now.
Example: 'You are free or this is free' regarding a slave.
5
Recognize metaphorical uses for generality
'Aw' can be used metaphonically to indicate generality: in negation contexts it requires individual application (each item), in permission contexts it allows combination (all items).
This affects rulings on oaths and exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حروف المعاني: حروف العطف ["أو" وحكمها]. وأما "أو" فتدخل بين اسمين أو فعلين فيتناول أحد المذكورين، فإن دخلت في الخبر أفضت إلى الشك، وإن دخلت في الابتداء والإنشاء أوجبت التخيير. ولهذا قلنا فيمن قال: هذا حر أو هذا، إنه لما كان إنشاء يحتمل الخبر أوجبت التخيير على أي هذا القول يحتمل أنه بيان حتى جعل البيان إنشاءاً من وجه إظهاراً من وجه، = أي هذا القول أيضاً. القيد فقط، فاندفع ما قال صاحب "غاية التحقيق" من أن في تلك الصورة أيضاً لا يتسق الكلام لأنه نفي فعل وإثباته بعينه. فتأمل. وذهب القاضي الإمام أبو زيد وأبو إسحاق الإسفراييني وجماعة من النحويين إلى أن كلمة "أو" للشك، وهذا ليس بسديد؛ لأن الشك باعتبار محل الكلام، لا أنها وضعت للشك، كما في قولك: جاءني زيد أو خالد كان المقصود هو الإخبار عن مجيئ أحدهما لكن بغير تعين، فوقع الشك بهذا الاعتبار لا أنها موضوعة له في الابتداء كما في قولك: اضرب هذا أو هذا. والإنشاء كقولك: هذا حر أو هذا، أوجبت التخيير لأن الشك الذي كان ينشأ من محل الكلام لا يوجد هنا؛ لأنه لإثبات الحكم ابتداء، فيعود إلى أصله وهو التناول لأحدهما من غير تعين. والأمر في الابتداء للايتمار، وهو لا يثبت بإيقاع الفعل في غير العين؛ لأن المأمور لا يعلم مراد الأمر، فثبت ضرورة التمكن من الايتمار. وكذا في الإنشاء لما تناول أحدهما غير عين أوجبت التخيير لدفع الإبهام. فالحاصل كما أن الشك في الإخبار يثبت من خارج كذلك التخيير في الابتداء والإنشاء يثبت من خارج لا أنها موضوعة لهما. ولهذا: أي لأجل أن "أو" لأحد الشيئين غير عين، وإنما يثبت الشك والتخيير بمحل الكلام. وقد تستعار هذه الكلمة للعموم، فتوجب عموم الإفراد في موضع النفي، وعموم الاجتماع في موضع الإباحة. ولهذا لو حلف لا يكلّم فلاناً أو فلاناً، يحنث إذا كلّم أحدهما. ولو قال: لا يكلم أحداً إلا فلاناً أو فلاناً، كان له أن يكلمهما جميعاً. وقد تجعل بمعنى حتى، في نحو قوله : والله لا أدخل هذه الدار أو أدخل هذه الدار الأخرى، فإن أو في هذا المثال بمعنى حتى.
Chapter on Particles of Meanings: Conjunctions - 'Aw' and its ruling. As for 'aw', it enters between two nouns or two verbs and denotes one of the two mentioned. If it enters into a statement (khabar), it leads to doubt; if it enters into a beginning (ibtida') or a performative (insha'), it necessitates choice. For this reason, we said regarding one who says: 'This is free or this,' that since it is a performative that admits the possibility of being a statement, it necessitated choice on any of these sayings. It is probable that it is a clarification, making the clarification a performative in one aspect and a statement in another. The same goes for this saying as well. Only the restriction remains, and thus refuted what the author of 'Ghayat al-Tahqiq' said: that in that case the speech does not also come together because it is negation of an act and affirmation of the same. So reflect. And Chief Judge Abu Zayd, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, and a group of grammarians held that the word 'aw' is for doubt, but this is not correct; because doubt is due to the context of the speech, not that it is placed for doubt, as in your saying: 'Zayd or Khalid came to me' - the intent was to inform about the coming of one of them but without specification, so doubt occurred through this consideration, not that it is placed for it initially, as in your saying: 'Strike this or this.' And the performative like your saying: 'This is free or this' necessitated choice because the doubt that arises from the context of speech does not exist here; because it is for affirming a ruling initially, so it returns to its origin, which is denoting one of the two without specification. And the imperative initially is for compliance, and it is not established by executing the act in a non-specific matter; because the commanded person does not know the command's intent, so the ability to comply is necessitated necessarily. Similarly, in the performative, when it denotes one of the two without specification, choice is necessitated to remove ambiguity. In summary, just as doubt in reports arises from external factors, similarly choice in initiations and performatives arises from external factors, not that they are placed for them. And for this reason - that is, because 'aw' is for one of two things without specification, and doubt and choice arise only from the context of speech. And this word may be used metaphorically for generality, so it necessitates generality of individual in a negation context, and generality of combination in a permission context. For this reason, if someone swears not to speak to so-and-so or so-and-so, he breaks his oath if he speaks to either one. And if he says: 'I will not speak to anyone except so-and-so or so-and-so,' he may speak to both of them. And it may be used in the sense of 'hatta' (until), as in his statement: 'By Allah, I will not enter this house or enter this other house,' for 'aw' in this example is in the sense of 'hatta'.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the particle 'aw' (أو) in Arabic, focusing on its legal implications in usul al-fiqh. The author first establishes that 'aw' fundamentally denotes one of two things without specification. When used in a report (khabar), it engenders doubt because the speaker does not specify which one occurred. In contrast, when used in a performative utterance (insha') such as a vow or declaration, it creates a choice (takhyir) for the agent to select one of the options. The example given is a person saying 'This is free or this' regarding two slaves; the utterance gives him the choice to free either one, not both. The author refutes the view of some grammarians who claim 'aw' itself indicates doubt, arguing instead that doubt is a consequence of the context. Then the passage explains that 'aw' can be used metaphorically for generality. In negation contexts (like oaths), 'aw' requires general application to each individual item, so an oath not to speak to one of two persons is broken by speaking to either. In permission contexts (like exceptions), 'aw' requires general combination, so an exception allowing speech to one of two permits speech to both. Finally, 'aw' can be used in the sense of 'hatta' (until) when the sentence implies a continuation up to a limit, as in the example of an oath to not enter a house until entering another house.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle of conjunction that denotes one of two or more things without specification.
شك (shakk): Doubt arising from the context when 'aw' is used in a report where the speaker does not specify which item occurred.
تخيير (takhyir): Choice given to the addressee when 'aw' is used in a performative (insha') such as vows, oaths, or declarations.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' denotes one of two unspecified items; its legal effect (doubt or choice) is determined by the context, not the particle itself.

The Particle 'Aw' (أو) in Negation and Permission
Analyzing 'aw' in negation, permission, and as metaphor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rules for the particle 'aw' (أو) to determine the legal effect in negation and permission contexts, and identify when 'aw' is used metaphorically as 'waw' or 'hatta'.

Core Idea
In negation, 'aw' requires falsity of each item individually; in permission, it allows all items collectively.

The particle 'aw' (أو) is a versatile conjunction in Arabic legal language. In Hanafi usul, its meaning is context-dependent: in negation (like oaths or prohibitions), it imposes individual generality (umum al-ifrad); in permission (like exceptions or grants), it imposes collective generality (umum al-ijtima). This lesson unpacks these two primary functions and also covers its metaphorical use as 'waw' (and) or 'hatta' (until) when the literal meaning is not feasible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Context
Determine whether the particle 'aw' appears in a negation (e.g., oath, prohibition) or permission (e.g., exception, allowance) context. The ruling hinges on this distinction.
Negation contexts include phrases like 'la af'alu' (I will not do) or 'la yajuzu' (it is not permitted). Permission contexts include 'illa' (except) or 'yajuzu' (it is permissible).
2
Apply the Hanafi Rule for Negation
In negation, 'aw' necessitates individual generality: each conjunct is considered independently. Thus, a prohibition or oath is broken by committing any one of the specified acts.
Example: Swearing 'I will not speak to Zayd or 'Amr' means speaking to either breaks the oath.
3
Apply the Hanafi Rule for Permission
In permission, 'aw' takes the meaning of 'waw' (and), necessitating collective generality: all conjuncts are permitted together. This is because the literal meaning of choice (one or the other) is impossible when the restriction is lifted.
Example: Saying 'I will not speak to anyone except Zayd or 'Amr' allows speaking to both.
4
Recognize Metaphorical Uses
When 'aw' cannot be taken literally (e.g., due to grammatical incompatibility or impossibility of conjunction), it is interpreted metaphorically as 'waw' or 'hatta' (until) based on contextual necessity.
For instance, 'I will not enter the house or I enter this other house' uses 'aw' as 'hatta' because conjunction is impossible.
5
Derive the Legal Effect
Based on the contextual interpretation, determine the actual legal consequence: number of oath expiations, permissibility of actions, or conditions for manumission.
Remember: with actual 'waw', multiple violations require multiple expiations; with 'aw' in negation, only one expiation is needed.

Source Text
